## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) is determined by restoring forces (dependent on x), damping forces (dependent on v), and possibly external driving (dependent on t). The nonlinearity can appear in the restoring force, the damping, or both.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (linear oscillator with periodic drive)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (c2 + c3 * x**2) (nonlinear damping dependent on position)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Damped pendulum: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (sinusoidal restoring + damping)
- Quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinear restoring)
- Quadratic-cubic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 + c2 * v (position-dependent damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-cubic damping)
- Driven Van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (c2 + c3 * x**2) + c4 * cos(c5 * t) (driven nonlinear damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) indicate symmetric potential wells; even powers (x²) indicate asymmetric potentials
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent energy dissipation or injection (damping/anti-damping)
- Position-velocity coupling terms like v*x² suggest amplitude-dependent damping (Van der Pol type)
- Sinusoidal dependence on position sin(c*x) indicates a periodic potential (pendulum-like systems)
- Explicit time dependence through cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) indicates external periodic forcing/driving
- Cubic velocity terms (v³) indicate Rayleigh-type nonlinear dissipation where damping depends on speed
- Negative linear damping combined with positive nonlinear damping (c1*v + c2*v*x²) creates limit cycle behavior
- The sign of the cubic coefficient in x³ determines whether the potential is hardening (positive) or softening (negative)
- Absence of explicit time dependence indicates an autonomous system where energy is either conserved or exchanged through velocity-dependent terms
- Combined quadratic and cubic position terms suggest a broken-symmetry oscillator with both even and odd nonlinearities
